Guild Jealousy Leads to Armed Fight

▲White Pine Gang and Bone Tile Industry

The bone tile industry in the city has a large number of manufacturing workshops and workers. A few years ago,洋莊 sold well, and the business was booming. Recently, foreigners have also set up factories to manufacture, so the business is not as good as before. Unexpectedly, recently, products made of white pine tiles have appeared, which are no less than bone tiles, and have a great potential to surpass them, causing jealousy from the bone tile gang. Therefore, the two sides have accumulated resentment and have repeatedly clashed. The Yuyuan Garden of the City God Temple is where the industry gathers. The other day, in the evening, both sides gathered dozens of people, armed with weapons, to compete for supremacy, launching a large-scale armed fight in the garden, as if facing a great enemy. The in-charge section of the first station of the first district heard about this and immediately sent the 通班长警 to rush to arrest them. The workers on both sides fled in all directions. The police immediately arrested six members of the White Pine Gang and three members of the Bone Tile Gang. Two of them were injured. The police took them all to the station for interrogation, and sent them to the Municipal Public Security Bureau overnight, to be transferred to the District Court for interrogation.

Recently, Zhuang Yushu was selling fake Golden Mouse brand cigarettes on Tiantong Road in Hongkou. He was detected by a detective from Huacheng Cigarette Company and immediately handed over to the police, and the counterfeiter Rong Chunlin was arrested, and many pieces of counterfeit cigarettes were seized. Special Item

Second Report of Mr. Tang (Continued 3)

▲ Summary Translation of the Fourth and Fifth Sections

▲ Chapter Four: The issues discussed herein are the four issues regarding the recovery of concessions mentioned in Chapter One. As stated above, the advocacy for recovery is based half on theory and half on practicality. Now, it is further revealed that those who oppose the concession system based on theory do so partly based on the origins of concessions and partly based on the nature of concessions. The arguments based on the origins of concessions are reviewed as follows: Those who support the demand for recovery sometimes regard the public concession system as established by the powers without the approval of the Chinese government and against the will of the Chinese government. However, I believe that the general public considers this view to be inconsistent with the facts. The Shanghai Municipal Council's handling of concession affairs is based on the Land Regulations, and the Land Regulations are effective because they have been agreed upon and approved by the representatives of the treaty powers and the representatives of the Chinese government. The detailed history of the Land Regulations described in a previous section of this report shows that except for the Land Regulations promulgated in 1869, which were not approved by the Chinese government, all subsequent promulgations of these regulations, or any important amendments thereto, as well as the final application of the current Land Regulations to the extended concession area in 1899, were agreed to by the Chinese government. Moreover, a study of the Land Regulations clearly shows that Chinese sovereignty within the concession was not only not abandoned but was also explicitly confirmed by the Land Regulations: the issuance of land deeds within the concession (Articles 2 and 3), the payment of annual rent to the Chinese government for "land leased by foreigners" (Article 8), and the provision that amendments or additions to the regulations, or any doubtful clauses, "shall be decided by the consul and the Chinese local officials in consultation, and shall be subject to the approval of the foreign minister and the highest Chinese government" (Article 28), are all clear evidence of the confirmation of Chinese sovereignty. However, on the other hand, it is important to note that although the Land Regulations explicitly confirm Chinese sovereignty within the public concession, and although the public concession system contained in the regulations has been agreed to by the Chinese authorities, the establishment of an institution by the powers within Chinese territory to exercise administrative power is, after all, a foreign intervention in the scope of power that a country always reserves for itself. Even if it is said that the representatives of the Chinese government participated in the adoption and promulgation of the Land Regulations in terms of facts, this does not yet provide a complete answer to the arguments based on the origins of the Land Regulations. It is also important to note that the origins and nature of the Land Regulations are at least partly based on the provisions of the treaties, which grant extraterritoriality to foreigners. In one sense, the Land Regulations are a product of the so-called "extraterritoriality," and from the perspective of Chinese critics, they are seen as being as objectionable as the extraterritoriality system. The situation of those who oppose the foreign nature of the public concession system is discussed as follows: Before the first Chinese directors took office in April 1928, the governance of the public concession, in terms of exercising the powers prescribed by the Land Regulations, was entirely in the hands of foreigners. All power was either in the hands of foreign ratepayers who had obtained the right to vote according to the Land Regulations or in the hands of a board of directors composed entirely of foreigners, who were elected by foreign electors. The inclusion of Chinese directors on the board fundamentally changed the nature of the public concession. Although the full effect of this change has not yet been felt or recognized, issues such as the employment of Chinese personnel in senior positions in the Shanghai Municipal Council and the publication of the Shanghai Municipal Council's documents and publications in Chinese have been re-examined in light of the new situation that has been created, and some important changes have been implemented regarding these issues. At the same time, further reform plans are being carefully considered. Regarding the arguments in favor of recovery based on practicality, an opinion was previously expressed and is now quoted here: the public concession system, if examined in terms of its actual results, is superior to any municipal system established in Chinese territory to date. The report also mentions that under the new circumstances, the issue of allocating municipal funds for the special welfare of the Chinese people has been raised, which shows that the current participation of Chinese directors in the council affairs is a more complete recognition of municipal cooperation between Chinese and foreign residents in the public concession. Regarding another aspect of the support for recovery based on practicality, it is discussed as follows: in terms of the unified administration argument, if the entire Shanghai area could be managed by one administrative body, there would be no doubt that it would benefit certain parts of the municipality, most notably the police and sanitation departments. However, the benefits of unification would depend on the nature of the unified administration under which the public concession and other municipal areas would be jointly governed. The report then summarizes and considers the opinions of those who oppose recovery. Now, let us discuss the arguments of those who oppose recovery. These arguments can be summarized as follows: (1) The public concession system established in accordance with the Land Regulations has been approved by the Chinese authorities and is stipulated in the treaties and various measures formulated to implement the treaties. These treaties and measures are still legally valid and effective. (2) Maintaining this system does not involve denying Chinese sovereignty within the public concession. (3) The security provided by the public concession is far superior to that of any area governed by the Chinese. Security has two meanings: (a) defense against foreign aggression and prevention of internal disorder; (b) adequate guarantees for the enjoyment of individual rights, including property rights. This feature of the public concession system is a fundamental requirement for the great commercial, banking, and industrial interests centered in the concession, and is therefore a fundamental requirement for Shanghai's current status as China's leading commercial and economic center. (4) In addition to security, the practical result of the public concession system is good governance, which greatly benefits Chinese and foreign merchants and residents within the concession, both past and present. The main reason for achieving this result is the exercise of the powers authorized by the Land Regulations by the foreign community.

Page 16

[H Fourth Sheet

The way in which the power authorized by the Land Regulations is used. (5) The circumstances that originally necessitated the establishment of the public concession system in accordance with the Land Regulations still exist. Under the current circumstances, if the public concession is handed over to Chinese administration, it is feared that the valuable results that the existing system has already achieved will not be maintained. In my opinion, the reasons that opponents of recovery can put forward, and which support the first four of the five points mentioned above, have been revealed by me when discussing the origins of the public concession system, the security it provides, other outstanding features, and the value of the actual results obtained. However, regarding the argument against recovery, if what I have stated is correct, it is important to note that this argument does not involve a demand that the public concession system established in accordance with the Land Regulations should be regarded as an immutable system. Opponents of recovery have indeed urgently stated that, under the current circumstances in China, there are strong practical reasons to oppose abolishing the existing system of the concession and handing it over to Chinese administration. However, if the situation changes and the Chinese government is able, by its own power, to establish a system within the public concession that can achieve the same results as the existing public concession system in terms of security, maintaining law and order, respecting private property rights, and good governance, it is not said that this new system should not be established. Therefore, the argument against recovery does not go so far as to assert that there are no theoretical reasons to support recovery. However, the point they are arguing is that even for the sake of satisfying the wishes of the Chinese people, the recovery of the concession must ultimately be carried out, but under the current circumstances, recovery is almost impossible because it will inevitably be followed by unavoidable unfortunate consequences. The report then suggests that the actual result of recovery depends on how the future government of the public concession will be established after recovery. Therefore, the second question, namely, what kind of new system will replace the old system after recovery, must be discussed. The points to be discussed are as follows: If, in reason, the best possible assumption can be made regarding the future system of the public concession after recovery, can the reasons held by those who oppose recovery as a practical policy for the near future of the public concession still be valid? Or can the immediate recovery of all difficulties be resolved if the Chinese government issues a charter, either solely for the public concession or together with other areas of Shanghai, based on the same principles as those currently in force in the public concession, and allowing the system of local autonomy to continue based on the cooperation of Chinese and foreign residents? The so-called "charter" means "a legal document issued by the National Government, which is effective by virtue of Chinese law, rather than relying on the measures contained in the treaties between China and the powers, and which stipulates that the Chinese community within the public concession will occupy a majority in the sole or multiple governing bodies within the concession." To know the effect of immediately recovering and issuing a charter, three further questions must be considered as follows: (A) Security is an essential element for maintaining Shanghai's status as a commercial center. Does the government established in accordance with the charter have the necessary power to continue to maintain various security conditions? What are the hopes for this government to exercise its power to maintain such security conditions? (B) What are the concrete guarantees for the permanence of this charter and the non-infringement of the autonomy it grants? (C) Is the local autonomy system established in accordance with this charter and controlled by Chinese votes a genuine local autonomy system, allowing the residents of the public concession to effectively exercise their right to independently handle affairs within the concession? To what extent can the outstanding features of the public concession system be maintained by this system? The report notes that the above three questions should not be considered in the abstract, but should be considered in relation to the current situation in China, and it is pointed out that question (A) has two aspects, because it involves two items: (1) What is the theory of the conditions that can be imagined and may be included in the charter? (2) What are the likely practical results of exercising the administrative powers conferred by these conditions? Question (A) is then discussed and answered as follows: (1) In terms of security relying on protection, if the international status of the public concession disappears and the functions of its governing body are based on the charter issued by the Chinese government, then the defense of the public concession will no longer be able to rely on the practical assistance of the powers, such as the assistance and dispatch of troops by the powers in times of crisis in the past. The special advantages previously enjoyed in terms of defense due to its international status will thus disappear. If a reasonable certainty cannot be obtained that the crises commonly seen in the past will not recur in the future, then replacing the existing system in accordance with the Land Regulations with a system established in accordance with the charter, no matter how well-equipped the public concession can be to defend itself under this new situation, the security within the concession will inevitably be reduced, with extremely serious consequences. (2) In terms of security relying on the rule of law, the governing body of the public concession organized in accordance with the charter may be granted a power that allows it not only to maintain the rule of law within the concession, but also to improve it. However, whether it can maintain and improve it depends on whether the right to exercise the power conferred is recognized by habit, and whether the governing body and its officials can abide by existing rule-of-law habits in the ordinary exercise of administrative power, and whether they can effectively implement the powers conferred in the charter. Question (B) is discussed as follows: If the charter of the public concession does not have a reasonable guarantee to ensure its permanence and non-infringement, then this charter is of no value to formulate. Any charter issued can be assumed to be contained in the laws enacted by the legitimate legislative body, or promulgated by the government in accordance with the provisions of these laws, but except for those stipulated in the treaties, nothing can prohibit this charter from being amended by subsequent legislation, or even revoked or amended by administrative action. Because under the current circumstances, there is no concrete constitutional guarantee to prevent the enactment of laws that abolish or amend it, or to cancel the charter by order of an administrative official. Before China's constitutional system is developed, and its courts are not only able to be independent of the administration, but also strong enough to enforce compliance with the law, even against the government itself, the above situation will continue. The same difficulties will also arise regarding the interpretation and application of the charter. The local autonomy charter given to Shanghai or the public concession must be interpreted by the Chinese courts, but before there are satisfactory guarantees of judicial independence, there is no guarantee that the powers given by the charter will not be arbitrarily deprived, or that the judicial decisions will not be influenced by the administrative or military authorities, so that these powers cannot be exercised. Even if Shanghai has its own courts, whose independence is specially guaranteed, these courts are not sufficient if problems arise between the local government and the National Government regarding the exercise of the powers conferred by the charter. Because if a problem arises, it must be decided by the national court. In addition to the lack of independence in the courts that interpret the charter, it is also important to note that the separation of government powers is based on law and can be enforced by the courts according to the division, but this concept is completely unfamiliar to the Chinese. The report then mentions a suggestion that the charter could include a provision to prevent the use of force to invade the area of local government and to restrict the National Government's power to levy taxes and special taxes in the area of local government, but it is pointed out that the courts have no power to protect this provision from being violated. "If there is no power to effectively implement the provisions of the charter, then the guarantees included in the charter are merely empty talk on paper. 'Security' cannot be built on this basis." The conclusion of question (B) is as follows: Therefore, under the current circumstances in China, unless treaty provisions are used to ensure that the affairs of the public concession are still handled by means of international cooperation, there is no effective provision to protect the powers conferred by the charter. Therefore, regarding the effectiveness and power of the charter, if the assumption that it relies on Chinese law, rather than on the measures contained in the treaties between China and the powers, is correct, then the answer to question (B) must be negative. Under the current circumstances in China, if any genuine local system is to be established in the public concession and thus give a security such as that given by the existing system of the public concession, its only appropriate basis is an international agreement.

Letters to the Editor

To the esteemed Editor: In the "Dongjiadu Catholic Church Bloodshed Case: Assassin Arrested" section of the local news column in your newspaper on the 18th, it stated that the church owns a lot of property and the monthly rental income is handled and managed by Father Lang. It also stated that when parishioners have weddings or funerals, they must pay at least several hundred yuan to hold Mass rituals in the church. After investigation, there are indeed several houses in the Dongjiadu area, which are owned by the General Church of the Nanjing Diocese of the Catholic Church. The rental income is used to supplement the various sub-churches, schools, hospitals, and charitable institutions throughout the Jiangsu Diocese. Dongjiadu is just one of the sub-churches in the diocese, and it has no right to collect rental income, let alone handle and manage it. Furthermore, when church members have weddings or funerals, even if they hold Mass rituals in the church, they are all voluntarily assisted by the parties concerned to supplement charitable expenses, and there is absolutely no need to demand hundreds of yuan. Your newspaper also called Qin Wenbin a cook in the church who was dismissed for poor cooking, which is even more unfounded. According to reports, Qin Wenbin is an ordinary servant in the church, not a cook. The occurrence of this incident was purely due to a villain harboring resentment and intending revenge. On the 4th of this month, the church happened to have a major feast day. The church was directed by Seminarian Zheng Xiu to direct the servants to decorate everything. Qin Wenbin was also among them. Because of his stubborn attitude and refusal to obey orders, Seminarian Zheng Xiu informed the priest and slightly reprimanded him. In the evening of the same day, Qin suddenly came to say goodbye, saying that he had obtained another job and would come to report tomorrow. The priest did not force him to stay because he voluntarily retired. However, he came again the next day to insist that the priest issue a letter of guarantee. The priest did not agree because of his usual improper behavior. Qin left reluctantly. Who would have thought that he would harbor resentment over a small matter, wield a knife, and cause the riot on the 15th? The above is all the factual situation, which is obviously inconsistent with what is reported in your newspaper. This matter concerns the reputation of the church and is for the sake of a true record of the news. I hereby submit this letter and request that you correct it as soon as possible. I deeply hope for this. Sincerely, The Dongjiadu Catholic Church, June 19.

To the Editor: I have read the section of your newspaper on June 17 regarding the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau's strict order to the Wusong Chamber of Commerce to dissolve within a time limit. After receiving the instructions from the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau, our association submitted a reply stating that there were still undisclosed circumstances to be reported and requested the Ministry of Industry to review the case. We have now received a response from the Ministry stating that there is reason to continue to exist and that we should wait for further instructions to be followed. Therefore, we will have to submit another request to the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau to maintain our existence. This is the first point that should be clarified. As for the various misunderstandings in the report in your newspaper about the party department's investigation into the collection of flag fees, they are too numerous to mention. However, what needs to be clearly understood is that the inspection of ships was an opinion put forward by our association for the sake of local security and contributed to the Jiangsu Provincial Department, as evidenced by the written report. Why falsely use the words "request from Zhejiang and Jiangsu shipping merchants?" The provincial government then deliberated on the measures and ordered the Fourth District of the Water Police Team of the Provincial Public Security Bureau to handle it. It can be seen that the inspection duties are entirely carried out by the Fourth District of the Water Police and have nothing to do with Shu Shan personally. How can he extort floating fees from various industries? Anyone with clear eyes can see this at a glance. How can such groundless rumors be aimed at individuals? This is the second point that urgently needs to be clarified. Gu Ningbo's Pig Industry Jinglan Guild sued Shu Shan for allegedly collecting flag fees. If it is not because of ignorance and being completely deceived by others, it is urgent to summarize the facts and ask your newspaper to correct them quickly to conform to the facts. Sincerely, Zheng Shushan, June 17.

The total number is 568 people. Among them, 253 people are for business matters, 146 people are for entertainment, 103 people are for fresh air, 53 people are for visiting relatives and friends, going to the theater, etc., 12 people are for traveling abroad, and only one person is for participating in sports.

▲ Due to the lack of doctors in West Africa, the British Colonial Office has specially sent many experienced female doctors to serve there. The starting salary for each person is 600 pounds sterling per year, with annual increments thereafter.

Detailed Record of the Anniversary of the Demise of the Premier in Guangzhou

— Sun Choucheng

The 16th of this month is the ninth anniversary of the demise of the Premier in Guangzhou. The Shanghai Special City Party Department specially convened people from all walks of life in the city to hold a memorial meeting in the Party Department auditorium. The next day, due to limited space in various newspapers, only a brief overview of the situation was disclosed. I attended and saw more details, which I will record as follows.

On that day, a bamboo cloth banner reading "Shanghai Commemorates the Ninth Anniversary of the Demise of the Premier in Guangzhou" was hung high at the entrance of the Party Department. The party and national flags were hung on both sides. In the auditorium, there was a huge half-length portrait of the Premier in a Western suit, surrounded by pine and cypress trees, adorned with paper flowers. The walls were covered with slogans such as "Continue the Premier's Spirit of Struggle" and "Continue the Premier's Spirit of Non-Compromise." Yang Qingyuan, the Minister of Propaganda, chaired the meeting and said that the Premier had devoted himself to the cause of national revolution for nearly forty years in order to achieve freedom and equality for China. The hardships and difficulties he went through are too numerous to mention, but the most prolonged and dangerous period was during the war in Guangzhou in the eleventh year of the Republic of China. This left a deep impression and a painful lesson on us. We should always regard it as the most inspiring and encouraging commemoration. At that time, Chen Jiongming controlled the military power of Guangdong and Guangxi, outwardly claiming to support the Premier but secretly opposing the Premier's policies. At that time, the Premier overcame all difficulties and personally led a large army to swear an oath to the Northern Expedition in Guilin. Chen then assassinated Comrade Deng Keng and cut off the military expenses for the Northern Expedition, wanting to put the soldiers on the front line to death. Later, because Zhao Hengti refused to allow passage, the General Headquarters moved to Shaoguan and returned to Guangdong, heading towards Jiangxi. Chen then secretly ordered his henchmen, Ye Ju, to besiege the Presidential Palace, occupy the institutions, and offer a reward of 200,000 yuan to harm the Premier. Someone secretly telegraphed the Premier in advance, asking him to leave the palace and take temporary refuge. Secretary Lin Zhimian also entered the palace that night to report. The Premier believed that even if Chen was evil, he would not resort to such rebellious and abnormal means of a traitor. Soon the rebel army approached, and Lin and others again urged the Premier to leave the palace, still willing to die for the country to thank the people. Seeing the urgency of the situation, Lin and others forcibly dragged him out of the palace and onto the Chu Yu warship. The rebel army attacked repeatedly. The Premier remained calm and composed throughout. Later, because the Northern Expeditionary Army was unsuccessful in suppressing the rebellion, he entrusted the task of pacifying the chaos to the support troops from various places. On August 8, he left Guangdong for Shanghai. The hardships and dangers he suffered during these fifty-odd days are countless. As a result, the rebel army could not harm the Premier's hair, and the Premier's revolutionary spirit and patriotic sincerity were more evident than the sun and the moon, and he was even more respected by the whole country. Today, commemorating the Demise of the Premier, we should associate it with the difficulty of the Premier's creation of the Republic of China. The situation we have today is all exchanged for the sacrifice of countless martyrs' heads and blood. Without consolidating unity, it is not enough to maintain peace. Now, the remaining warlords and idle politicians are gathering in Guangzhou again, and the evil communists are rampant in Jiangxi, all of which are obstacles to the Republic of China. I hope that people from all walks of life will unite to support the provisional constitution of political tutelage, overthrow the new warlords who endanger the party and the country, and consolidate peaceful unity. Everyone applauded. Then, two proposals were passed, and slogans such as "Commemorate the Demise of the Premier in Guangzhou" and "Eliminate All Reactionaries" were shouted before the meeting adjourned.

Tidbits

— (Cuckoo)

Heartbroken and devastated are originally exaggerated adjectives used by poets and lyricists for those who are heartbroken in love. But people who are in love have at least three kinds of illnesses: insomnia, indigestion, and inexplicable depression.

Wonderful Sayings Picked Up

— Cai Liang

Mr. Pan Guangdan spoke of the three words "eugenics." In the minds of our esteemed countrymen, I fear this concept has not yet made an impression. However, Westerners have already applied it from humans to various animals. What mare has mare caretakers, cow has cow maids. Regarding the selection of seeds, there is extremely deep research. Look at the horses in the Shanghai Racecourse, all so magnificent and extraordinary. This is powerful evidence. Other things can also be imagined. If we talk about our poor and weak nation, we will naturally be bullied by others everywhere. Because in their eyes, we are simply not even as good as cattle and horses. Speaking of this, don't you think it's painful? Therefore, as I see it, if a nation wants to survive in the current world, especially a backward country like China, it is even more necessary to vigorously study "eugenics." When the race is truly improved, the country will naturally become strong without needing to be forced.

Foreign Folk Remedies of a Medical Doctor

— Ms. Ye Hua

Dr. Fei Kunnian, who served as a physician in various public hospitals in Germany and Austria for more than ten years, recently returned home to visit his relatives. I was troubled by poor appetite, so I went to Dr. Fei's residence at No. 9 Parker Road to seek advice. I obtained the Austrian folk remedy of adding tea to meals, and after trying it, it worked like magic. Later, I met Mr. Fei again, and we discussed many Western folk remedies. I now record the essential ones for the benefit of readers.

▲Adding Black Tea to Meals: Whenever we encounter sluggish digestion or poor appetite due to weakness or overwork, the way to remedy it is to drink a cup of strong black tea on an empty stomach every morning. Add a large amount of white sugar to the tea, making it even sweeter and more palatable. It is even acceptable if the ratio of sugar to tea is half and half. After taking it for ten days, one should be able to have a better appetite than usual.

▲Salt Water to Stop Thirst: After exercise or work, we often sweat profusely and feel extremely thirsty. Drinking any liquid only increases abdominal bloating and does not relieve thirst. Thirst is actually a mixed sensation of touch, warmth, pressure, and dryness. The reason is a lack of saliva flow and a deficiency of water and salt in the body. If you drink a cup of salt water, saliva will naturally be produced.

▲Beer to Sober Up: Those who are overly fond of drinking often get drunk. The next day, they still feel dizzy and disoriented. If they drink a little more wine, they will feel refreshed and return to normal. This is commonly called "revival wine." If you drink a glass of cold beer, the effect is even more pronounced. It is also good to use freshly squeezed lemon sugar tea instead of wine.

▲Hiccups and Nasal Congestion: If the throat is occasionally subjected to special stimulation, hiccups will follow. Hold your nose, stop breathing, and drink several mouthfuls of warm tea water at the same time to cure it. In the early stages of a cold, if nasal congestion is unbearable, boil lemon juice, add sugar, and drink a cup while it is hot to clear the nose and feel comfortable. If you feel unwell and your pores are tightening, indicating that illness is about to strike, drink a large glass of cold water with a drop of iodine tincture to prevent it. However, the amount of iodine should be small rather than large. An excess of one drop can harm the body.

Research on Famine Relief Food (Part 2)

— Tianxu Wosheng

The third recipe says: "Seven sheng of black beans and three sheng of sesame seeds. Wash them with water and steam them immediately. Do not soak them for too long. After steaming, dry them in the sun, remove the shells, and steam them again, repeating the steaming and drying three times. Grind them into pills the size of longans. Take one pill per serving. It will prevent hunger for three days." I believe that the nutrients contained in chestnuts and walnuts are more abundant than those in glutinous rice and sesame seeds, and black beans are even more abundant than chestnuts and walnuts. I will list them as follows:

Item Name Fats Water Carbohydrates Protein Fat Starch Remarks

Chestnuts 174.14 22.8 218.94 Each catty is equivalent to 4 catties and 11 taels of rice

Walnuts 170.94 355.14 19.14 Each catty is equivalent to 4 catties and 12 taels of rice

Black Beans 204. 108. 138. Each catty is equivalent to 5 sheng and 6 he of rice

From the above list, it is clear that the effectiveness of the second recipe is greater than that of the first recipe, and the third recipe is even better. Every year when the year ends in Hangzhou, we must wrap zongzi with glutinous rice. The fillings are divided into several types. Black beans are skinned, stir-fried into a paste, and called "Yuansha," which is the third recipe. The roughly made ones are mixed with black beans and glutinous rice and called "black-eyed pea zongzi." Or the beans are mashed into a paste without removing the skin and called "bean paste," all for the sake of being easily filling. Or chestnuts are mixed with glutinous rice and called "chestnut zongzi," which is the second recipe. Those with jujube paste as filling are the first recipe. Those with glutinous rice flour as the outer layer and filled with sesame seeds and walnuts combine all three recipes. The same principle applies to "Washing Sand Soup" or "Bean Paste Steamed Buns." These are all foods that people often eat, so why should there be any doubts?

Strange Marriage Customs

— Qin

Yesterday, I met an old friend, Mr. So-and-so, who is a soldier. During our meeting, he described the marriage customs of women in Tingzhou, Fujian, which were quite interesting. I quickly recorded them to fulfill the purpose of free discussion.

The women of Tingzhou are very open-minded, beautiful, and intelligent. Even during the Qing Dynasty, they had already abandoned the bad habit of foot-binding.

During the three years between the ages of seventeen and nineteen, they choose their spouse. Every time they encounter the Lantern Festival, Dragon Boat Festival, Mid-Autumn Festival, and other festivals, they all dress up elaborately and go out to seek a mate. If they find someone they like, they can invite him home and tell their parents. Their parents will treat him like an honored guest, offering him auspicious foods such as lotus seed soup and glutinous rice balls, hoping that the two of them can be united and have many children. On this day, the man will stay at the woman's home.

If the woman believes this man is reliable, she will announce her marriage to him. Even her parents have no right to interfere. On the day of the wedding, all the men who have been invited home by the woman in the past (those who were rejected) should present a folding fan with their name inscribed on the left side, half-opened, and arranged on the ceremony table. The bridegroom's fan will be fully opened and placed in the center. The number of fans represents the woman's eligibility. More is considered an honor, while fewer fans cause discontent.

The houses in Tingzhou are very large, and many have bamboo curtains. When there is nothing to do, women hide behind the curtains to look at the scenery outside. If a man sees them, regardless of whether he knows them or not, he can enter and talk to them.

There is a stream in that area, with peach blossoms planted on both banks. When the flowers are in bloom, the stream water often turns red, hence the name Peach Blossom Stream. It is also a strange sight.

The material is even more exciting. Newspaper vendors are distributing it. For those in other cities who want to subscribe, please send a letter with postage to 231 Lloyd Road, Shanghai. (Wang Yanjin)

Rotary Club Literary Association

Three Eras (11)

— Zhang Henshui

(5) The Second Enemy

Zhang Xiaosan became a soldier not only because he wanted to make a name for himself, but also because he was angered by his wife, Zhang Ersao. Zhang Ersao always said, "If I can't find an official, can't I find a rickshaw puller?" Zhang Xiaosan thought to himself, "I can't read and I don't have money, how can I become an official?" This was ultimately what led his wife to look down on him. Later, he thought of the storytellers' tale of Xue Rengui, who also came from a poor background. "Why can't I learn from him?" he thought. "If I want to become an official, the only way is to become a soldier." Thinking this, he was persuaded by a recruiting speaker at Tianqiao and immediately joined the army. After joining the army, he realized that becoming an official was not an easy task. He had joined the army to prove himself, but unexpectedly, things were even worse than before. All of this was caused by his runaway wife. He hated her even more. The policeman was Zhang Xiaosan's enemy, and he finally vented his anger by beating him up. His second enemy was his wife. He wanted to find her and give her a beating. But after she ran away, he didn't know where she was hiding. How could he find her? Time passed quickly, and in the blink of an eye, a year had passed. One day, Zhang Xiaosan set out with the army. He was in the baggage train, escorting two large carts of luggage. As the carts passed through Tianqiao and out of Yongdingmen, he encountered his second enemy at the Tianqiao head. She was not the same as before. Her hair was combed sleekly, and her face was covered in white powder. She was wearing a floral print cheongsam and swaying as she walked along the road. Behind her was a man in a long gown, walking and smiling with her. Zhang Ersao kept turning her head back, laughing and talking to him. When Zhang Xiaosan saw this, he wanted nothing more than to grab the rifle on his back and shoot them both, first killing Zhang Ersao and then the man with her. However, there were officers in front and behind, and he not only dared not fire his gun but also dared not leave the column. He could only glare at Zhang Ersao. As he glared at her, Zhang Ersao also looked at him, took the man's hand, and whispered something. The two of them then disappeared into the crowd. Zhang Xiaosan was filled with hatred. The man's face looked familiar. He had seen him somewhere before. That's right. He was the messenger from the house of Li, the deputy minister in the same alley. His wife used to wash clothes for him. So it was him who had seduced her and run away. "One day, when I get my hands on him, I'll have him shot," he thought as he followed the column. Before he knew it, he had passed through Yongdingmen. Outside Yongdingmen was the countryside, no longer Beijing. He was over thirty years old, but he never thought that leaving Beijing would be like this. He also thought that this time he was leaving Beijing to fight with Inspector Zhao. Whether he would return or not was uncertain. Thinking this, he couldn't help but turn his head back and take another look at the city walls behind him. He felt a strange reluctance in his heart. In fact, everyone in the city, from the President to the 1.3 million residents, had nothing to do with him. And there were also his enemies and rivals in love.

Continued Small Decline in Financial Gold Prices

▲Slight Fluctuation Results in Slight Drop: Yesterday, the 19th, the gold price continued to be slightly sluggish, with slight fluctuations. From morning to evening, a total of six taels of money were recalled. In the end, it fell by about two liang. The silver market remained stable, with a high opening, and foreign exchange seemed strong, with unchanged postings. Afterwards, the sellers in the market showed courage, resulting in a drop from high to low. The market suddenly fell to the 800-liang mark, which was indeed a sign of active selling, but there were no large transactions. However, the exchange rate stood firm. It is said that the amount of each company's orders was about 50,000 yesterday at noon.

▲High at the Beginning and Low at the End of the Morning Market: The opening price in the early morning of August rose by 1 liang and 1 qian to 803 liang and 5 qian. Large bars and silver prices were as before. Private telegrams were slightly lower by one-sixteenth. However, the market was sluggish, and the buying interest of various companies was still strong. Companies such as Taichang, Yuanmaoyong, Tianfengyong, Fuyu, Yuanxingyong, and Xinheng all made purchases, so the price rose again by 2 liang. When the exchange rate stabilized, Lihui, HSBC, Mitsui, Citibank, etc., all offered 25 for British gold in July and August. Maijiali took over 25 to 3125. The announcement of British gold remained unchanged, with the price at 06 liang. Subsequently, companies such as Yuda, Yuanmaoyong, Yuanxingyong, and Futaiheng all sold, resulting in a drop of about 2 liang to 04 liang and 1 qian after 10 o'clock. Companies such as Tongtaichang, Hengyu, Dadecheng, Yuanheng, Chunyong, and Qianchangxiang all bought, and recently British gold banks took over 25. Meifeng and Mitsui mutually traded US dollars at 28.875 yuan, and the market price surged by 2 liang and 56 qian, reaching 06 liang and 8 qian at nearly 11 o'clock. Afterwards, the exchange rate was stable, and it was estimated that British gold could still be settled at 25. Companies such as Bingxing, Daxingyong, Dadecheng, Longsheng, Yuanmaoyong, Hengxing, and Yuanxingyong poured sales onto the market, resulting in a sluggish trend and a drop of 3 liang and 78 qian. The posted price was still estimated at 838 liang and 2 qian, with a premium of 33-34 liang to more than 31 liang. The morning closing was 35 liang.

▲The Afternoon Market Went from Flat to Soft: The afternoon market opened at 03 liang and 5 qian, followed by 4 liang and 3 qian, and then decreased slightly to 3 liang and 8 qian. However, the transaction was very small. Then small investors came in, and it rose to 04 liang and 8 qian. After 2:30, companies such as Tongfuyu sold, retreating to 3 liang and 7 qian. After 3 o'clock, Wanxing, Qianchangxiang, Yuanmaoyong, etc., bought in, and at 3:30, it was 05 liang. Afterwards, it seemed to show a softening trend, slightly less than 1 liang. However, there were not many transactions on the table. Until 3:45, there were reports of large Indian exchange transactions of 4.5 Anna, and Longsheng and Yuanmaoyong continued to sell, resulting in a further reduction of more than 1 liang to 01 liang and 3 qian at 4 o'clock. It immediately returned to 2 liang and 23 qian. Then, companies such as Fuyuyongfeng sold, and the market further declined, depreciating by 2 liang, suddenly becoming 800 liang 002 qian. However, British gold remained stable, and banks continued to take over 3125. The closing price at 4:30 was 800 liang 006 qian, and then it was raised by 1 liang to 01 liang and 78 qian, a further drop of 1 liang and 8 qian compared to the previous day (according to the posted price). According to the whole market, the highest price was 806 liang and 8 qian, and the lowest price was 800 liang 002 qian, with a difference of 6 liang and 6 qian. The article says that the morning market was 3 liang and 8 qian, the noon closing was 4 liang, the afternoon was 4 liang, and the closing was 1 liang. The listed price was estimated to be a premium of 33-34 liang to 37-38 liang, with account entries of 06 liang in July and 03 liang in August, a water supplement of 06 liang in the afternoon, and 04 liang.

▲Transactions Were Not Active: Companies such as Taichang bought more than 2,000 lots, which was to cover the previous day's short positions. Zhifengyong, Fuyu, Tianfengyong, Yuanheng, Yuanmaoyong, and Xinheng all bought in. Yuancheng, Bingxing, Hengxing, Futaiheng, Yongfeng, Yuda, and Daxingyong all sold. However, tomorrow is a Sunday, and banks and gold exchanges are usually closed, so the market will not reopen until the 22nd.

The Yarn, Cotton and Cloth Market Is Tight

▲Yarn Sales Remain Very Smooth

The yarn market is very firm and the rising trend is very strong. In fact, the demand for existing yarn is becoming more and more enthusiastic. The procurement from the north is unusually active. The 16-count and 20-count yarn from our factory have been completely bought out, and there are no existing goods to buy. They have changed to buying futures for July and August, which shows the enthusiasm of the various gangs. This situation is completely affected by the exchange rate. The north has always been occupied by Japanese yarn. Recently, because the price of Shanghai yarn is quite cheap and the sales of cloth in that area have also improved, there has been a large amount of inflow. Therefore, the sellers see that the factories' existing goods have been emptied and the various gangs continue to come to purchase and make up for losses. The situation in the market is very tight. If the current sales continue uninterrupted, the price of yarn may reach a new high. It is also possible that there will be a period of fluctuation in the middle.

▲People's Standard Rises 6-7 Qian: The opening of the People's Standard price in the morning fell with the decline in foreign cotton. People's hearts were slightly tired, and each fell by 6-7 qian. Then, at the second session, the market atmosphere suddenly tightened. Because there was a lack of sellers, the market became very tight. Prices for each month rose by 3, 4, 6, and 8 qian. The market atmosphere remained strong in the afternoon, and the closing was slightly tired, with each rising by 1-3 qian. The transaction volume was 61,700 bales. It was found that Dafu sold 1,450 bales, Gongtai sold 1,450 bales, Tongyu sold 1,550 bales, Gengfeng sold 4,300 bales, Shenchang sold 1,850 bales, Yongfeng sold 2,450 bales, and Yichang sold 1,450 bales. Jifeng bought 1,200 bales, Shenxin bought 1,950 bales, Tianlong bought 2,250 bales, Changfeng bought 2,700 bales, Yiyu bought 1,300 bales, Deki bought 1,100 bales, and Taixing bought 1,200 bales. Silk, Tea, and Foreign Firms: Silk Market Continues to be Firm

In European and American markets, sales from Chinese silk factories are gradually picking up. However, Japanese silk opening prices are not high, making it difficult to expect continued price increases for electro-spun silk, and transactions are not smooth. Yesterday, only Xinfu and others imported 40 bales of Shanghai white factory silk, and Samsung and others imported 20 bales of yellow coarse silk. Prices are still firm.

Summer Silkworm Diseases Discovered in Hangzhou

In Gaosi, Sanbao, Linping and other places in Hangzhou, summer silkworms were hatched early this year and the feeding amount was increased to make up for the shortage of spring cocoons. Since entering summer, the weather has been sunny and warm, which is very suitable for silkworm rearing. The ants hatched quite evenly and developed smoothly. The early batches have already entered the third sleep and started eating leaves. However, since the day before yesterday, after two days and nights of moldy rain, the temperature dropped sharply, and the silkworm ants underwent changes. Farmers were careless in feeding the leaves, and the silkworms ate wet leaves, causing diarrhea. The instructors are now trying to isolate the affected silkworms.

Qimen Black Tea Sales to Europe Improve

Yesterday, the black tea from Qimen's upper and middle villages, including Tianyu, Jinlong, Xingcheng, and Dued, all started operations, and transactions became more active. Sales prices ranged from 57 taels to 170 taels, 20 to 30 taels lower than last week. The overall trend of Luzhuang Zhenmei green tea remains sluggish. In yesterday's market, first-class firms in England, France, and Japan only had a slight appetite for core-extracted Zhenmei, with little activity for the rest. Although a small number of Wuyuan North Road goods arrived in Shanghai for sampling, the market has been poor recently, and dealers are demanding strict prices, so no new quotations have been released. The future of green tea is difficult to be optimistic about.

Grain and Rice Markets Affected by Rainy Weather

▲ Xin Zha, Yesterday

About twenty ships arrived at various wharves on Lu Road. Market sales have become more active due to the moldy rain. In addition, most cargo owners have suffered heavy losses and intend to sell to recover their costs. Top-quality Changshu Beigeng rice remains flat, while second-quality Zhongguan Suxi rice rose by 2 jiao. Early and late rice from sand boats sold well on the road, and the situation also improved by about 1 jiao. The glutinous rice market is mediocre, without any rise or fall. Foreign Dujian rice and local imports are still strong, and transactions of top-quality Dujian are not weak, with the situation tightening. Although the supply of Dujian and Kejian rice is limited, it is still available, and there are no major changes in the overall market.

▲ Shanghai South

Yesterday morning, the weather was windy and rainy, and the arrival of goods at various wharves remained sparse. Sales in local shops were even slower, and there were few customers. Due to the rain, Hehe rice was scarce, and the supply of fresh rice continued to increase, stabilizing the price. Given this moldy market, the situation is stable. The sales of thin rice are ordinary, and although foreign Dujian rice is scarce, the appetite for it is sluggish, and the market is weak. Through changes and adjustments, workshops are still buying in large quantities, so the situation has dropped by 1 jiao. The opening for each type of rice was 600-700 dan. Today is the Lunar Dragon Boat Festival, and both the North and South markets will suspend rice transactions for one day.

Woolen Piece Goods and Fine Serges are Soaring

The woolen piece goods market is rising rapidly. Yesterday, fine serges in particular showed a strong upward trend. In recent days, Sichuan merchants have been actively purchasing, and yesterday Tianjin and Changsha also showed activity. In addition, overseas quotations are rising steadily, leading to exceptionally good sentiment among holders of goods. Yesterday, prices rose by about 1 fen each. Sanyou Tu Changjiang merchants sold at 3 qian 4 fen 7 li and a half, Tu Yuan also reached 3 qian 3 fen and a half, Huxin Ting 3 qian 5 fen and a half, Baoqiu 3 qian 9 fen 7 li and a half, Gucheng 4 qian. Lower-quality goods such as Qianliju, Gongsun Tu, and Hele Tu are even more scarce. Zhigong woolen cloth also rose, with Zhuhu reaching 3 qian 1 fen and a half, Sanyou Tu Dongmian selling at 3 qian 5 fen, and Lieyan also being in short supply. Moqianshan has reached 3 qian 8 fen and a half. The futures market for Sima Xiangru's Yangtze merchants is also strong. White ting cloth and white hemp yarn, which had previously declined, have now turned from falling to rising, due to speculators taking the opportunity to purchase. Yesterday, ting cloth was around 2 qian, and hemp yarn has all gone out of customs at 2 qian. Fine cloth has been rising sharply in recent days due to the surge in local factory goods, and eastern goods have also seen sharp increases. Yesterday, Shile Bird was at 9 taels and 7 qian and a half, and Yueyan was at 10 taels and a half.

North-South Goods: Definite News of Poor Harvest of Jinshan Chestnuts

▲ Market Price is One-Third Higher than the Current Market

News of the scarcity of new Jinshan chestnuts and poor harvest has been spreading in Shanghai for some time. According to reliable sources, the price of fresh chestnuts has already been set. If they are processed into dried chestnuts, they will have to be priced one-third higher than the current Shanghai market price. Therefore, merchants in Shanghai who have old stock are unwilling to sell them cheaply, and the trend is very firm, with expectations of further price increases in the future.

Sugar Market: Rising Prices in Japanese Car Sugar Market

Yesterday's sugar market reports from producing areas: the price of Cuban spot sugar was 1.34375, a slight increase of 0.03125 compared to the previous telegram. The price of New York sugar futures was 1.30 for September, 1.39 for December, 1.46 for March next year, and 1.53 for May, all up 3 points compared to the previous day, except for March, which was up 2 points. The price of Javanese sugar futures remained unchanged. In the exchange market, the buying interest for Dutch sugar No. 24 was very quiet, with the offering price at 11 taels and 7 qian, and No. 20 medium-sized white sugar at 11 taels and 1 qian, both with few inquiries. No. 10 Dutch red sugar was at 9 taels 9 qian 7 fen and a half, and the goods were not high, but the market sentiment was very strong. The Japanese sugar market saw a slight increase, with Z mark at 11 taels 2 qian and a half, SH mark at 11 taels 1 qian and a half, TM mark at 11 taels 2 qian 2 fen and a half, YT mark at 11 taels 3 qian to 3 qian 2 fen and a half, YP mark at 11 taels 7 qian, YPO mark at 10 taels 9 qian 7 fen and a half to 11 taels, Taikoo DY mark at 11 taels 2 qian to 2 qian and a half, and B mark at 11 taels and a half. Youth Corner

After Seeing "The Liar"

— Jingzhai

Speaking of the two words "drama" inevitably makes us think of the so-called year of drama – just passed the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, in this year, the drama movement was truly at its peak. Although the result of this effort did not give us satisfying achievements, it may not be that it did not give us some new enlightenment regarding the drama movement. This, in our immature art scene where everything lags behind, especially in the aspect of dramatic art, is always a fact worth being joyfully optimistic about. However, in our country where everything is unfortunate, it seems that there is a god presiding over everything. All undertakings only have a fleeting fate. Our drama movement also failed to pass this stage and eventually declined with the passing of the year of drama. How sad this is for those who care.

Recently – after the call for the drama movement has been silent for a long time – our movement, which has suffered many setbacks, has begun to move in various aspects again. The unrestrained nature of this trend has greatly formed a phenomenon of revival or restoration. As far as we know, the earliest is the public performance of "A Patriot's Heart" by the Jing'e Drama Society, the public performance of "Mei Luo Xiang" by the Zhonggong Drama Society, and the Su Ni Drama Society is preparing for a public performance. These all indicate a vigorous atmosphere. In particular, the eleventh public performance of "The Liar" by the Fudan Drama Society is the most prominent and largest in scale.

The Fudan Drama Society, as they themselves said, "slowly transformed from the nature of recreation to a purely research drama art group." The reason why they have achieved this result is really due to their environment – Fudan University has a hard-working academic atmosphere, and the drama courses offered by Fudan University are complete. With this, in this innate and thick element, a "Cyrano" child that caused a sensation was born. Following this child, what was conceived and born was "The Liar," the public performance that I am going to talk about now, whose reputation is no weaker than that of his brother "Cyrano."

"The Liar" is said to be a flawless work by Jones, a complete comedian from England. Judging from the name, of course, what is expressed in this play is the fact of "lying". But it is not entirely so. Now, in order to make it easier for readers to understand, I might as well give a brief explanation here.

The cause of the matter is that a love story that young people often perform occurred between Mr. Zhang Jingkai, who had just come to Shanghai from Nanyang, and the wife of Mr. Ye Menghua, a giant merchant in Shanghai. Naturally, this matter was not approved by the friends and relatives of both parties. They all came up with many ways to persuade these two protagonists, but as a result, the persuasion failed. Later, by coincidence, these two lovers met in a hotel. Naturally, the coincidence mentioned here is just a lie. At the same time, even more coincidentally, Mrs. Ye's husband's brother also came at this time. So this matter was about to get big. In order to save these two protagonists, their friends decided on a lie that could justify itself after careful deliberation. But unfortunately, the lie was exposed again. In this way, this matter was almost brought to an irreparable situation. But Mr. Lin Wangxian, a friend who was smart, experienced, understood everything, and knew everything, seized the opportunity at this time and did not let it go, finally making this couple, who was about to break up, reconciled again. And Mr. Zhang Jingkai, who was originally a heroic and daring passionate lover, also woke up from the dream of love, knowing that there were more important tasks on his shoulders than love, and ended his own romantic play.

Although the content of this script has so many twists and turns, it has completely conveyed it in only four acts. Therefore, in each of its acts, there are many tense flavors buried. So if we are just standing on the position of drama to speak, then this "Liar" is indeed a very perfect good work with the magic of attracting people. But if we think that the success of an artistic work must grasp the spirit of the times and be able to promote a social effect, then this "Liar" is just a common story. In addition to obtaining considerable effects in terms of technology, it did not show any great significance. This is because we did not find an amazing great character and miracle in this play. Every character and every accident in it is just rolling around in the strong and stubborn traditional social morality network. This is inevitably going to make people feel a little pity.

Regarding the plot of this "Liar", I have said some above. Now let's talk about other aspects.

The success or failure of a play is related to the actors. I think I don't need to say more. This is the first important thing that everyone knows. When we make an overall observation of the actors in "The Liar" this time, it is indeed very rare, worthy of neatness and not bad criticism. But if we want to make individual criticisms, then the one that I want to mention first is not the two protagonists, but a key role, Mr. Tang Xuanfan who plays Lin Wangxian. Although it is said that this gentleman's disguise as a ghostly hermit is still an attempt, we have to admit that he has reached the point of success. Although we can't say that he is perfect, his lines are so thoughtful and fluent, and his demeanor is so leisurely and unrestrained, everywhere showing that he is a well-thought-out and worldly-wise figure. At the same time, he also carries a lot of interesting expressions. This role is really too suitable. This is the most outstanding of these many actors. The next thing to say is of course the female protagonist, Ms. Li Lian, who plays Mrs. Ye. Ms. Li is indeed a rare person with stage talent. The role she played in this play is also very appropriate. Except that she speaks too fast and all her actions and actions have committed a flaw of being too impetuous, everything else can give people a satisfactory comfort. Speaking of Ms. Liang Peiyu, then we should still remember the female protagonist in "Cyrano". Yes, this is an all-rounder with a very generous and calm attitude, very delicate and thoughtful expressions, and very mellow and clear lines. It is a pity that because her position in the play is not very important, we have not been able to fully look up to all her strengths. The other ladies can also do it in an orderly manner, suitable for their own position in the play, although small flaws are also inevitable, especially Ms. Lv Manyun who plays Miss Ma, her facial expressions are worthy of being top-notch, especially her charming eyes. But it is a pity that her attitude is too lacking in dignity, and she has also committed the fault of being too much. It is inevitable that she lacks the humorous and shy demeanor of being a young lady. If this were replaced by a woman who is good at charming and used to showing off her style, then this expression would be praised endlessly. As for the male roles, generally speaking, they can still be competent. However, Mr. Wu Zhongmin, who plays Zhang Jingkai, has too few facial expressions. There is always a tone on his face, and there are few opportunities to make people distinguish that he has expressions of joy, anger, sorrow, and happiness. This is his personal shortcoming. If Mr. Kong Lingjue, who plays Ye Menghua, is the worst in degree among these key roles. In short, the neatness of the actors this time is considered very rare.

We know that the meaning and mission of the drama club movement is not only to mature in technical aspects, but also to end the matter. Its greatest and most important meaning is that it can produce a social effect. Therefore, here, all our comrades who are working hard in the drama movement must know that our success is in many aspects, containing a central consciousness. The fit of the performance, the beauty and profoundness of the plot, these are still secondary issues. Therefore, if we ask the gentlemen of the Fudan Drama Society, do they also think so?

(1) The content of the text should be related to discussions on youth issues, news about domestic and foreign schools or students, essays, descriptions of school life, notes, etc., and the style is not limited.

(2) The pictures are limited to those related to youth issues.

Letter Received

Treating Diseases with Jiashu

— Xu Sifang

Since I entered the world, I have been down and out, depressed and sad, so a lump rose on my chest, like a stone egg, and occasionally when I felt it, it swelled and pained like a chicken egg. It was a blessing if it did not swell or hurt at ordinary times. I have been treated by famous Chinese and Western doctors, but it was ineffective. It has been more than ten years. Recently, I returned to Shanghai from Zhejiang Province after resigning from my post. Touching the present and feeling the past, I felt sad everywhere, and the lump broke out severely. I thought it had been accumulated for a long time and it was difficult to heal. It should not be treated with medicine, and I could only wait to die. Then I read a newspaper saying that Yu Dian Passerby, No. 18 Simingli, (at the intersection of Xiafei Road and Luban Road in the French Concession,) advertised for treating diseases with Jiashu, and I felt that it was sincere and moving, not comparable to the common quacks who lied to the world. Moreover, because I could not bear the pain, I sincerely went to seek treatment with my roommate. I felt that the room was clean and pleasant. I registered and was invited into the upstairs room. I saw a person sitting in the middle, about thirty or forty years old, twisting prayer beads in his hand, with a calm and solemn expression, and respectful appearance. I asked his name, and he was Mr. Lao Jingdian from Hunan. He kindly said to me, "Jia is Yin and Yang. Jiashu is using Yin and Yang numerology to relieve suffering. It cannot be said that it can be effective if you start. It also depends on the fate of the person seeking treatment. We only use the scriptures to cultivate the Tao and visit friends. Therefore, we must first ask for the eight characters of the year of birth to see if there is fate. In particular, the person seeking treatment must make a wish. Our Taoism is based on abstaining from killing and releasing life as its purpose. If you cannot immediately observe vegetarianism, you must make a wish to abstain from killing one living creature, no matter how big or small, according to your wish, or swear to abstain from killing one cow, or one snail. You must swear that you will never eat this one cow or one snail for the rest of your life before you can be treated. Therefore, we are aware that in modern times, morality has collapsed, and we sincerely hope to use this to prevent friends and jointly maintain this Taoism. People in the world do not know the hard work of the ancient sages and saints in establishing the Tao and saving the world. They fail to know the preciousness of our country's philosophy, and use the two words 'superstition' to generalize and obliterate, which leads to the concealment of the great Tao. Therefore, we want to widely seek people with fate to cultivate the great Tao together." Then he said that the symptoms are painful, because the Qi and blood are not smooth, so if it is smooth, it will not hurt. It must be that the body feels wind, fire, phlegm, and dampness, which obstruct the flow of Qi and blood, so it causes pain. The treatment is to remove these four diseases to dredge the Qi and blood and make them flow smoothly without obstruction. Two Taoist talismans should be drawn with a cinnabar pen (divided into You talisman and Jia talisman), and taken home at 11 o'clock at night. Burn three incense sticks, prepare a basin of clean water, first burn the You talisman, and then swear at that time to abstain from killing any living creature, then burn the Jia talisman in the clean water, and then take three mouthfuls of water. The pain should stop, and come again in three days. He should talk about the principles in detail, and give a plaster to paste under the human character bone, that is, the affected area. He said that if after pasting, you feel that the pain is getting worse, and there is sticky liquid sucked out from the affected area, it is a good phenomenon. It does not hurt to wipe the liquid away and paste it again. This is to gather the disease in one place and expel it through the pores. If the pain does not increase, then the effect is not effective, and come again in three days. Surgery should be used to massage or acupressure to treat it. The intention of the surgery is also to gather the disease in one place and expel it. Sometimes, it is necessary to cut the skin a little to provide an outlet. This is a simple way, and it is also a fundamental way to eliminate it. Then he took it home and pasted it. One day, he unconsciously increased the pain, and he also felt that the usual pain was lost. The so-called sticky liquid was exposed, but it was not seen. After three days, he went again, and Mr. Lao used surgery, slightly massaged, and cut the skin a little with a small knife. A reddish-brown sticky liquid flowed out, about a teacup, and the disease was lost as if nothing had happened. It was really magical. According to him, this liquid was formed by accumulated diseases. Now he is ordered to continue to paste the plaster on the affected area, and go again in three days to examine my constitution. If it is not healthy, I am still afraid that the disease has not been cleared, and all three times, the disease will be removed. The only cost is one yuan for the first registration, which is to pay for the servants. Yu Dian Passerby and Mr. Lao are dedicated to saving the world, borrowing the Tao to visit friends, and working together to create the great Tao, maintaining the philosophy passed down by the ancient sages and saints, so that people can get rid of diseases and extend their lives. Every day, I hear their servants say that only three people are allowed. I dare to use my own experience to swear to prove that it is not like a quack who lies to the world and borrows techniques to collect money. I also heard that men and women can be cured of various diseases, and the premise is whether there is fate. It is said that the great Tao is mysterious and subtle, and people dream. Those who have fate, one finger points out the maze, and they immediately realize. Those who have no fate, the great Tao is in front of them, and there is no way to follow. This news is difficult to explain in words without prior wisdom.
